  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_529a323d-5d1f-4de2-904f-ade9a96c5041'
      });
    }

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2946722648" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2946722648" />
    <a title="Henry Avila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5431458-henry-avila"><img alt="Henry Avila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307597403p2/5431458.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2946722648?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Henry Avila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Henry Avila" href="/user/show/5431458-henry-avila">Henry Avila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781934609842" href="/book/show/11252863-a-man-lay-dead">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2946722648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15724005952614928909">This being the first Roderick Alleyn murder mystery... out of 33, of Ngaio Marsh, wonderful appellation, ( beats the first name of Edith... her middle one tops that, no contest) the author is getting her sea legs the plot nothing new even in 1934 when written. Sir Hubert Handesley invites a small number of guests for the weekend, a party of British frivolities, eating, drinking, walks in the woods and even a mock killing in his huge country estate , Frantock Hall; silly fun and games, companions</span>
  <span id="freeText15724005952614928909" style="display:none">This being the first Roderick Alleyn murder mystery... out of 33, of Ngaio Marsh, wonderful appellation, ( beats the first name of Edith... her middle one tops that, no contest) the author is getting her sea legs the plot nothing new even in 1934 when written. Sir Hubert Handesley invites a small number of guests for the weekend, a party of British frivolities, eating, drinking, walks in the woods and even a mock killing in his huge country estate , Frantock Hall; silly fun and games, companionship in the fresh air away from tumultuous London. However things become dark soon as the pretend murder isn't but horrid reality... a dead man on the floor refuses to rise, the fun ends immediately. Nigel Bathgate a reporter arrives by train with his older cousin Charles Rankin a man who likes the ladies and they reciprocate. Mr. and Mrs.Wilde, Arthur, Marjorie, he an archaeologist with a shaky marriage, a mysterious Russian art expert Foma Tokareff nobody trusts and last but as we say not the least, beautiful Angela North a friend of Rosamund Grant the niece of Sir Hubert .Where would a murderer be without a police detective? Free, not in this genre . ..Enter the gentleman Roderick Alleyn from London's Scotland Yard where else... still he looks befuddled and ordinary is this an inspector the suspects since everyone inside the mansion and outside is one, the guests , servants, the maids , butlers , cooks and gardeners aren't immune to the investigation either, tiresome, meticulous though it seems to them... afraid of...certainly... However a budding romance between Angela and Nigel sparks the rather glum atmosphere otherwise and gives relief to the harsh proceedings .The inspector sends the two brave or naive a better word, into a dangerous assignment against foreign criminals, a gang hesitant they're not to break the law for profit or benefit, connected to the murder.This mystery gives a lot of false clues about the identity of the real murderer and too many scenes outside the main place of interest you can say convoluted, still a good entertainment and having read another of the writer's books Alleyn #16 in the series , "Night of the Vulcan", become better as they go along... published during the height of the classic mystery era...my own opinion I could be wrong and often am, who doesn't like a mystery except the deceased...victim.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15724005952614928909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_227478431" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227478431" />
    <a title="Mir" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/237469-mir"><img alt="Mir" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275489063p2/237469.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227478431?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mir" href="/user/show/237469-mir">Mir</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/237469-mir?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227478431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15478202242973523918">Marsh introduced her famous detective in this mystery, and you can tell that she wasn't entirely sure what personality to go with. At times he reads like Wimsey playing a silly ass, at other times he is crude or clever in the manner of a Bright Young Thing; he takes the official police hard-line one moment only to suddenly behave in unprofessional and even inappropriate ways. I suspect she was trying to write realistically complex character, but the overall effect is one of schizophrenia and imp</span>
  <span id="freeText15478202242973523918" style="display:none">Marsh introduced her famous detective in this mystery, and you can tell that she wasn't entirely sure what personality to go with. At times he reads like Wimsey playing a silly ass, at other times he is crude or clever in the manner of a Bright Young Thing; he takes the official police hard-line one moment only to suddenly behave in unprofessional and even inappropriate ways. I suspect she was trying to write realistically complex character, but the overall effect is one of schizophrenia and implausibility. <br /><br />Luckily, we spend most of the story from the point of view of Nigel Bathgate, a somewhat two-dimensional Nice Young Man of the sort that one would let date one's sister (but probably find too boring to have a relationship with). There's no pomo unreliability here; it is clear that he is innocent, and his requisite wholesome love interest is dismissed from suspicion, apparently out of convenience to the romance subplot. Otherwise, the victim and suspects are sufficiently unpleasant that there is no sense of urgency about the solution.<br /><br />Most interesting to me, partly because it is so dated, is the side mystery with the Bolshevik conspirators. Did you know that in addition to being dirty communists they practiced weird, vaguely Satanic rituals that sometimes culminate in self-immolation? No? Neither did Marsh. The only thing the police really seem to be after them for is publishing seditious literature, which I guess every contemporary reader was assumed to consider a serious and despicable crime. Bolshies! Don't let anyone give you one of their sacred ritual daggers or they will track you down* and murder you!<br /><br />*It won't be difficult; you'll happen to be at the weekend house-party of a mutual friend. I don't know why anyone still goes to house-parties in England, it is just asking for trouble.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15478202242973523918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1556517420794944306">Now I am way behind with my Ngaio Marsh challenge , not because I was delaying reading these books, but for other book reasons. So when I started reading this book I was hoping I would enjoy it, and I did. I have seen a few TV episodes with Patrick Malahide, but had no pre-conceived ideas of Chief Inspector Alleyn, that said, I must admit he did come across very Patrick Malahide -ish.<br/>My previous book was another detective story <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18114335.Pietr_the_Latvian__Maigret___1_' title='Pietr the Latvian (Maigret, #1) by Georges Simenon' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pietr the Latvian</a> and it was to me a fantastic, albeit short detecti</span>
  <span id="freeText1556517420794944306" style="display:none">Now I am way behind with my Ngaio Marsh challenge , not because I was delaying reading these books, but for other book reasons. So when I started reading this book I was hoping I would enjoy it, and I did. I have seen a few TV episodes with Patrick Malahide, but had no pre-conceived ideas of Chief Inspector Alleyn, that said, I must admit he did come across very Patrick Malahide -ish.<br />My previous book was another detective story <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18114335.Pietr_the_Latvian__Maigret___1_" title="Pietr the Latvian (Maigret, #1) by Georges Simenon" rel="nofollow noopener">Pietr the Latvian</a> and it was to me a fantastic, albeit short detective story; If that is the epitome of a detective story (and I did give it 5 stars, as I have some Holmes stories) then this is a definite 4 stars. Given that I have signed up to read 12 Ngaio Marsh novels this year (so yes I am way behind) a 4 star enjoyable read is a good start and I look forward to the next 11 books in the series, bring it on.</span>

<div id="review_1753349191" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1753349191" />
    <a title="Carol She&#39;s So Novel꧁꧂ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25867535-carol-she-s-so-novel"><img alt="Carol She&#39;s So Novel꧁꧂ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575603145p2/25867535.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

  <span id="freeText11670542754950416796" style="display:none">2.5 ★<br><br>&amp; that high only because this was Marsh's first book. Makes you realise what a remarkable achievement Christie's first , <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/816084.The_Mysterious_Affair_at_Styles__Hercule_Poirot___1_" title="The Mysterious Affair at Styles (Hercule Poirot, #1) by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a> was.<br><br>Other reviewers have criticised Marsh for inconsistencies in Alleyn's characterisation. I actually don't mind this. I prefer it to having Alleyn &amp; various aristocrats angsting over being involved in something as low bred as a <i>murder!</i> This is very tedious in Marsh's other novels. And I did enjoy the start- although for some strange reason, the frenetic pace had me imagining everyone saying their lines while dancing 30s style.<br><br><blockquote>

</blockquote><br><br> Marsh's theatrical background always makes me see her characters as actors playing a part, rather than as three dimensional humans.<br><br>Like many of Mary Stewart's books, there was another character in this one.<br><br><blockquote>

I hope, in time, they will forgive me!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/553914725?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/5837456-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13344723-a-man-lay-dead">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer553914725" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5075036535364573514">This is the first of Ngaio Marsh's Roderick Alleyn mysteries and it contains everything that a great Golden Age mystery should. First, the house party, complete with varying guests - an adulterous wife, jealous girlfriend, mysterious Russian, etc. In this case, the country house in question is Frantock and Nigel Bathgate (a journalist) is accompanying his cousin Charles on one of the much coveted entertaining weekends, for which invitations are hard to obtain. The host, avid collector, Sir Huber</span>
  <span id="freeText5075036535364573514" style="display:none">This is the first of Ngaio Marsh's Roderick Alleyn mysteries and it contains everything that a great Golden Age mystery should. First, the house party, complete with varying guests - an adulterous wife, jealous girlfriend, mysterious Russian, etc. In this case, the country house in question is Frantock and Nigel Bathgate (a journalist) is accompanying his cousin Charles on one of the much coveted entertaining weekends, for which invitations are hard to obtain. The host, avid collector, Sir Hubert Handesley intends to hold a 'murder' game, which naturally goes completely wrong, when there is a real victim. <br /><br />Alleyn is a great character, who involves Nigel Bathgate and Sir Hubert’s niece, Angela North, in his investigation. What follows is lots of implausible plot twists (via the Russians) and an even more implausible conclusion, but the whole thing is great fun. Ngaio Marsh does not cheat and you could, if you are extremely clever and keep notes, work it out. Personally, I was happy to relax in her highly competent hands and enjoy. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5075036535364573514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3339400812" />
    <a title="BrokenTune" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10592271-brokentune"><img alt="BrokenTune" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391017756p2/10592271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3339400812?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BrokenTune" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BrokenTune" href="/user/show/10592271-brokentune">BrokenTune</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3339400812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15435319481949824923"><i>Alleyn looked at him with a curious air of compassion.<br/>‘Not even yet?’ he said.<br/>‘Whose were the prints?’<br/>‘That I am not going to tell you. Oh, believe me, Bathgate, not out of any desire to figure as the mysterious omnipotent detective. That would be impossibly vulgar. No. I am not telling you because there is still that bit of my brains that cannot quite accept the QED of the theorem.</i><br/><br/>Well, that was one of the silliest GA detective stories I have read. Not bad or horrible or totally off-putting, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText15435319481949824923" style="display:none"><i>Alleyn looked at him with a curious air of compassion.<br />‘Not even yet?’ he said.<br />‘Whose were the prints?’<br />‘That I am not going to tell you. Oh, believe me, Bathgate, not out of any desire to figure as the mysterious omnipotent detective. That would be impossibly vulgar. No. I am not telling you because there is still that bit of my brains that cannot quite accept the QED of the theorem.</i><br /><br />Well, that was one of the silliest GA detective stories I have read. Not bad or horrible or totally off-putting, but entirely implausible. So, implausible that I even want to call it "cute".<br />So, when Alleyn stated (see quote above) that the QED had not been established, yet, I may have laughed out loud. I may also have laughed again at the end of the book.<br /><br />I am glad I have read A Man Lay Dead after having already another of Marsh's books, because I already know that Marsh can write a splendid mystery. It's just that A Man Lay Dead is not it.<br /><br />Now that this first book is out of the way, I look forward to the rest of the series, tho.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15435319481949824923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1435215766" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11775299913683477747">It is New Zealand November and I am trying to read more books from and about New Zealand as part of my year-long Oceania reading spree in 2015.<br/><br/>Ngaio Marsh is a well-loved crime writer from New Zealand, but most of her books are set in and around London. Her Inspector Roderick Alleyn series seem (from this first one) to be the light whodunits along the lines of Agatha Christie. Over-the-top characters, some big words I had to look up (some just being regional words we don't use in the USA), silly</span>
  <span id="freeText11775299913683477747" style="display:none">It is New Zealand November and I am trying to read more books from and about New Zealand as part of my year-long Oceania reading spree in 2015.<br /><br />Ngaio Marsh is a well-loved crime writer from New Zealand, but most of her books are set in and around London. Her Inspector Roderick Alleyn series seem (from this first one) to be the light whodunits along the lines of Agatha Christie. Over-the-top characters, some big words I had to look up (some just being regional words we don't use in the USA), silly tied up ending. A fun read but nothing to do with New Zealand!<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_277455628" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/277455628" />
    <a title="Wealhtheow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76129-wealhtheow"><img alt="Wealhtheow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1178337774p2/76129.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/277455628?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wealhtheow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wealhtheow" href="/user/show/76129-wealhtheow">Wealhtheow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer277455628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16563604323010141368">A young reporter is enjoying an upper-class British house party when abruptly, someone is found dead! <br/><br/>I can't say I enjoyed this. There's an entire subplot concerning a Bolshevic satanic cult (?!) <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[that goes nowhere, and isn't even an effective red herring. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This is the first Inspector Alleyn book, and it's clear that Marsh isn't sure how to write him yet. His personality is all over the place: one moment he's burbling Bright Young Things slang, the next he's cold an</span>
  <span id="freeText16563604323010141368" style="display:none">A young reporter is enjoying an upper-class British house party when abruptly, someone is found dead! <br /><br />I can't say I enjoyed this. There's an entire subplot concerning a Bolshevic satanic cult (?!) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that goes nowhere, and isn't even an effective red herring. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This is the first Inspector Alleyn book, and it's clear that Marsh isn't sure how to write him yet. His personality is all over the place: one moment he's burbling Bright Young Things slang, the next he's cold and remote, the next he's romantically morose. It doesn't read like a complex character so much as one without any fixed characterization. The mystery itself is very frustrating, because there's no way it should have worked. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The murderer springs out of the bath, pulls on gloves, slides down a bannister face-first, yoinks a dagger conveniently nearby, and stabs his victim who just so happens to be standing with his back directly in front of the bannister? No one on earth would plan a murder that way! And there's no way that Alleyn figured out that the murderer did it that way, when his only evidence was that the murderer wore a glove! How does <i>that</i> prove that someone slid down the bannister face-first, let alone which person did it? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Ridiculous! <br /><br />I'll try one more Marsh book, by virtue of her reputation, and then I think I'll call it quits.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16563604323010141368" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review277455628">

<div id="review_2185862203" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2185862203" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5837456-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372225128p2/5837456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2185862203?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/5837456-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2185862203" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer73173635973409545"><br/>This is the first of Ngaio Marsh's Roderick Alleyn mysteries and it contains everything that you expect from a Golden Age mystery. First, the house party, complete with varying guests - an adulterous wife, jealous girlfriend, mysterious Russian, and more. In this case, the country house in question is Frantock and Nigel Bathgate (a journalist) is accompanying his cousin Charles on one of the much coveted entertaining weekends, for which invitations are hard to obtain. The host intends to hold a </span>
  <span id="freeText73173635973409545" style="display:none"><br />This is the first of Ngaio Marsh's Roderick Alleyn mysteries and it contains everything that you expect from a Golden Age mystery. First, the house party, complete with varying guests - an adulterous wife, jealous girlfriend, mysterious Russian, and more. In this case, the country house in question is Frantock and Nigel Bathgate (a journalist) is accompanying his cousin Charles on one of the much coveted entertaining weekends, for which invitations are hard to obtain. The host intends to hold a 'murder' game, which naturally goes completely wrong, when there is a real victim. <br /><br />There are lots of implausible plot twists (via the Russians) and an even more implausible conclusion, but the whole thing is great fun. Apparently, Marsh herself was embarrassed by this, her first, mystery, but she need not have been so. Although this was published in 1934, meaning that Christie, Sayers and Allingham all had books published before her (in the 1920’s), she quickly became a huge success and has remained one of the four major Queens of Crime. I have read very few of her books, but I intend to remedy that this year, and have certainly enjoyed this first in the series. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="73173635973409545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_169586161" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/169586161" />
    <a title="Abbey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4437424-abbey"><img alt="Abbey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1287504365p2/4437424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/169586161?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abbey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abbey" href="/user/show/4437424-abbey">Abbey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/35171268-a-man-lay-dead">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4437424-abbey?shelf=vintage">vintage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4437424-abbey?shelf=myst-cosies">myst-cosies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4437424-abbey?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4437424-abbey?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4437424-abbey?shelf=myst-set-andor-auth-uk">myst-set-andor-auth-uk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4437424-abbey?shelf=myst-fems-project">myst-fems-project</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4437424-abbey?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4437424-abbey?shelf=myst-police">myst-police</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer169586161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7617295821646809288">BOTTOM LINE: Thoroughly old-fashioned "good read!", with an aristo-detective, all the suspects gathered in A Great House for a weekend house party, a peculiar murder method, wild Bolsheviks complicating everything, family intrigues galore, an affable-but-dim Watson - what's not to like? First mystery novel (1934) from a now-classic author isn't challenging, brilliant, or particularly special, but is still entertaining, giving a hint of her good books yet to come and, as is usual with Marsh, ther</span>
  <span id="freeText7617295821646809288" style="display:none">BOTTOM LINE: Thoroughly old-fashioned "good read!", with an aristo-detective, all the suspects gathered in A Great House for a weekend house party, a peculiar murder method, wild Bolsheviks complicating everything, family intrigues galore, an affable-but-dim Watson - what's not to like? First mystery novel (1934) from a now-classic author isn't challenging, brilliant, or particularly special, but is still entertaining, giving a hint of her good books yet to come and, as is usual with Marsh, there are nicely pointed sly digs here'n'there.<br /><br />Nigel Bathgate's cousin Charles is a bit of a dog - loving the pursuit of ladies rather too much, he enjoys playing with fire, and gets burned, in many ways. He loses a girlfriend/possible wife (who truly loves him) while in pursuit of an already-married woman, whose current husband isn't much pleased. And while remaining rather likable (at least in callow Nigel's eyes) his superscilliousness and air of "I know better/all!" gets on not a few raw nerves during an extended house party. And not many are surprised when, in the course of A Murder Game, he winds up truly dead - and in a spectacular (how like Charles!!) fashion. <br /><br />Enter Inspector Alleyn - obviously refined, very well-educated, extremely likable, his smooth demeanor hides a mildly tormented psyche, as he finds he must expose Nice People to the machinations of the police force and its subsequent events, some not at all well-mannered. With these attributes Alleyn, in Marsh's first novel, is quite ordinary, an oft-used character in popular novels of the time, and although in future novels he becomes a rather interesting personality with a fascinating backstory, in this his first recorded case he is quite traditional, and rather stodgy. And while in subsequent novels Marsh builds up the cast of regulars around Alleyn (especially the wonderful Mr. Fox), here he's pretty much the entire show, except for a funny local policeman named Bunce - yet another character that often shows up in mysteries from the 1920s and early 1930s. <br /><br />The plotting, while good, is also quite ordinary for the period - a stilted setting, a twisted murder mystery with overlapping elements of several crimes, a bit of spy-thriller nonsense, some slight omnipotence from the police, and a thoroughly ludicrous bit of play-acting-cum-reconstruction of the crime at the end. But it's all very smoothly written, and while now a curiosity, at the time "this sort of thing" was quite popular. <br /><br />Now considered one of the Queens of Crime of the period (along with Christie and Allingham), Marsh's first mystery is still enjoyable, if not special or especially thrilling. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7617295821646809288" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3285987432" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3285987432" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3285987432?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/21938800-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/25590436-a-man-lay-dead">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21938800-john?shelf=ngaio-marsh">ngaio-marsh</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3285987432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14055354780169967247">This is Ngaio’s first Roderick Alleyn novel and it is a good introduction to the series I am slowly working through in no particular order. The story is set at Sir Hubert Handsley is well-known country house, Frantock where he is having a murder mystery party. He has invited his friend invited Charles Rankin a bachelor who likes the ladies and is a bit of a scoundrel and managed to annoy everyone he meets. <br/><br/>The other guests include: Charle’s cousin Nigel Bathgate a journalist; Rosemund Grant who </span>
  <span id="freeText14055354780169967247" style="display:none">This is Ngaio’s first Roderick Alleyn novel and it is a good introduction to the series I am slowly working through in no particular order. The story is set at Sir Hubert Handsley is well-known country house, Frantock where he is having a murder mystery party. He has invited his friend invited Charles Rankin a bachelor who likes the ladies and is a bit of a scoundrel and managed to annoy everyone he meets. <br /><br />The other guests include: Charle’s cousin Nigel Bathgate a journalist; Rosemund Grant who is in love with Charles; Angela North the fast driving niece of Sir Hubert, and Arthur and his wife Marjorie Wilde, Arthur is a writer and archeologist who Charle’s bullied at Elton and and his attractive wife. There is also Dr. Tokareff a Russian involved in a secret brotherhood, a few maids and an elderly and Russian butler called Vassily. <br /><br />Everyone is gathered for the murder mystery weekend and then someone is actually killed with a dagger with links to Russia. There are quite a few motive including money from inheritance, an angry lover, an angry husband and breaking the rules of the brotherhood. The Russian sub plot is a good twist. <br /><br />In this first novel Alleyn is not fleshed out with no real details of his background. It’s a good mystery if a like far fetched in how the murder is actually done. It made me laugh although I am sure that was not the intention. Overall a good read set in 1934. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14055354780169967247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2242621404" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2242621404" />
    <a title="Bruce Beckham" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28623020-bruce-beckham"><img alt="Bruce Beckham" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442874525p2/28623020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2242621404?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bruce Beckham" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bruce Beckham" href="/user/show/28623020-bruce-beckham">Bruce Beckham</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2242621404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6895645304129662827">I’m a soft touch for pre-war murder mysteries set amongst the English upper classes, so I guess this novel – published in 1934 – was always going to offer some vicarious appeal.<br/><br/>As kids, before heading off to school, my pals and I used to rendezvous on our bikes outside the village bookshop (imagine – a village bookshop!). I recall displayed in the window paperbacks by the exotically named ‘Ngaio Marsh’. I don’t know what I thought they were about, but I can’t believe it has taken me so many deca</span>
  <span id="freeText6895645304129662827" style="display:none">I’m a soft touch for pre-war murder mysteries set amongst the English upper classes, so I guess this novel – published in 1934 – was always going to offer some vicarious appeal.<br /><br />As kids, before heading off to school, my pals and I used to rendezvous on our bikes outside the village bookshop (imagine – a village bookshop!). I recall displayed in the window paperbacks by the exotically named ‘Ngaio Marsh’. I don’t know what I thought they were about, but I can’t believe it has taken me so many decades to discover they are of my favourite genre.<br /><br /><i>A Man Lay Dead</i> is the author’s first of her gentleman detective series, featuring the educated and erudite Roderick Alleyn. My main assessment – and I can fully empathise with the predicament – is that at this stage in her writing career she had little idea of how to construct a murder mystery.<br /><br />The setting and the characters – the country house party, the well heeled and even better connected circle of associates – spot on. But the plot – ouch! – she certainly loses it at times, and there is one flapping great red herring of a diversion in the middle of the story.<br /><br />Notwithstanding, the first two pillars carry the day, and – since (I read on Wikipedia) there are 32 books in the Roderick Alleyn series – I am looking forward to the shoring up of the third.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6895645304129662827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7517173677543146335">A reread of an old favorite. Ngaio Marsh's first novel, this story takes place in an English country house where a parlor game of "Murder" results in a real murder committed with a real dagger. Chief Detective Inspector Roderick Alleyn comes to the rescue and eventually figures out whodunit. In this cast of well-drawn characters, my favorite was the naive young journalist Nigel Bathgate, who, at 25, "had outgrown that horror of enthusiasm which is so characteristic of youth-grown-up."   <span id="freeText7517173677543146335" style="display:none">A reread of an old favorite. Ngaio Marsh's first novel, this story takes place in an English country house where a parlor game of "Murder" results in a real murder committed with a real dagger. Chief Detective Inspector Roderick Alleyn comes to the rescue and eventually figures out whodunit. In this cast of well-drawn characters, my favorite was the naive young journalist Nigel Bathgate, who, at 25, "had outgrown that horror of enthusiasm which is so characteristic of youth-grown-up." I love rereading Golden Age mysteries, and fortunately I have all of Marsh's books in paperback, so I can revisit them whenever I like!<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12180685943906024942"><i>
  <b>"It's going to be Murders this time."</b>
</i><br/><br/>A group of friends meets at Frantock Hall, Sir Hubert Handesley's country house, where they want to play the Murders game.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>One person is chosen as the murderer, his identity being concealed from all the players. They scatter, and he seizes his moment to ring a bell or bang a gong. This symbolizes the “murder”.</b>

  <span id="freeText12180685943906024942" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"It's going to be Murders this time."</b>
</i><br /><br />A group of friends meets at Frantock Hall, Sir Hubert Handesley's country house, where they want to play the Murders game.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>One person is chosen as the murderer, his identity being concealed from all the players. They scatter, and he seizes his moment to ring a bell or bang a gong. This symbolizes the “murder”.</b>
</i><br /><br />A murder is thus announced and one of the guests lies dead. <br /><br />It was easy enough to guess who the intended victim and the murderer are. The same cannot be said about the absurd way the homicide is committed, which is really unbelievable. Also I was not particularly happy with how Yard Inspector Alleyn comes to the solution of the case, because I got the impression that much is kept from the reader.<br /><br />The beginning is fast paced, but then the story starts to drag and I found "The Russian Element" part rather boring. The ending was quite satisfactory to me, though.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1303360849" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1303360849" />
    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1478144-john"><img alt="John" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442450473p2/1478144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1303360849?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/1478144-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312963583" href="/book/show/835695.A_Man_Lay_Dead">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1303360849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1480262674242869891">Gossip columnist Nigel Bathgate is invited to a weekend house party at the country home of ex-diplomat weapons collector Sir Hubert Handesley. Among the other guests are: an opinionated Russian scholar, Doctor Tokareff; the mild-mannered Arthur White; and Nigel's middle-aged cousin Charles Rankin, a roue who's having an affair with White's wife Marjorie, also there, while still being in a relationship with yet another of the guests, Rosamund Grant. Sir Hubert's niece Angela North is also among t</span>
  <span id="freeText1480262674242869891" style="display:none">Gossip columnist Nigel Bathgate is invited to a weekend house party at the country home of ex-diplomat weapons collector Sir Hubert Handesley. Among the other guests are: an opinionated Russian scholar, Doctor Tokareff; the mild-mannered Arthur White; and Nigel's middle-aged cousin Charles Rankin, a roue who's having an affair with White's wife Marjorie, also there, while still being in a relationship with yet another of the guests, Rosamund Grant. Sir Hubert's niece Angela North is also among the company, and soon she and Nigel have taken a shine to each other.<br /><br />Sir Hubert proposes that on the Saturday evening they play a game of Murder. The butler will randomly select a guest to be the "murderer"; between 5.30 and 11.00 the "murderer" must tell another of the guests that s/he is the "corpse"; the "murder" thus having been committed, the "murderer" must go to the hall, sound the gong there and throw the main switch for the house's lighting. The "murderer" then has two minutes to make an escape in the darkness to another part of the house. Once light's restored, the guests are to use their ratiocinative powers to deduce the identity of the culprit.<br /><br />You're way ahead of me. That evening the gong sounds and, when the scattered guests arrive in the hall, they discover the murder is for real. Stretched out in front of the gong is Charles Rankin, stabbed through the heart by a ceremonial knife he'd brought to the house with him to show Sir Hubert.<br /><br />Enter Inspector Roderick Alleyn . . .<br /><br />This was the first of the Alleyn mysteries, and it has some unpolished edges; for example, Marsh can't decide if Alleyn's a Detective-Inspector or has the nonexistent rank of Inspector-Detective. (It's odd that her publisher didn't correct this for her.) In an essay by Marsh that I read a few months ago, she recounts how she dreamt up Alleyn as a sort of response to the other aristocratic detectives whose exploits were at the time forging bestsellers. Like Wimsey and Campion, then, Alleyn has a light-hearted, foppish surface persona that's at odds with the steely intellect beneath. This persona, I know, gets the backs up of some readers, and I recently saw quoted with loathing a line of Alleyn's from <i>A Man Lay Dead</i>:<br /><br /><blockquote>"You've guessed my boyish secret. I've been given a murder to solve--aren't I a lucky little detective?"</blockquote><br /><br />In the book itself, however, the line appears in a context that gives it a very different color:<br /><br /><blockquote>"What's the matter with you?" said Inspector Boys. "Has someone found you a job?"<br /><br />"You've guessed my boyish secret. I've been given a murder to solve--aren't I a lucky little detective?"</blockquote><br /><br />In other words, Alleyn isn't being a fey fathead: he's responding in kind to a bantering remark. Whether cops in the real world would ever speak like that is a different matter. But in Golden Age mysteries we don't expect our detectives to be especially realistic. Wimsey? Poirot?<br /><br />Marsh actually has a sly dig at this trope in the text:<br /><br /><blockquote>"My only information [about police detectives] is based on detective fiction," said Nigel.<br /><br />"So is mine," Rosamund laughed silently, shrugging up her thin shoulders. "And nowadays they make their Yard men so naturalistic that they are quite incredible. This man Alleyn, with his distinguished presence and his cultured voice and what-not, is in the Edwardian manner. He hectors me with such haute noblesse it is quite an honour to be tortured. . . ."</blockquote><br /><br />From the arrival of Alleyn onward, the plot really divides into two. One strand concerns the provenance of that ceremonial dagger and its connection to Russian/Polish secret societies currently active in London. There's some great fun to be had with this strand, although in truth it's merely a red herring. The other strand is of course the solution of the murder. Here Marsh plays pretty fairly with us, although the actual technique used by the murderer is, while feasible, quite absurd, especially given the fact that the foul deed had to committed opportunistically rather than being carefully planned in advance. In this, of course, Marsh was once again conforming to a fairly standard Golden Age practice.<br /><br /><i>A Man Lay Dead</i> is a tremendous romp. It's a short book by today's standards, and I galloped through it in a single evening -- well, the evening did run a tad late. I didn't actually guffaw at any point, but I did chuckle quite often, and I did enjoy some of the characterizations. There's a delightful sort of Pre-Code feeling to the proceedings, too.<br /><br />All in all, splendid entertainment.<br /><br />=====<br /><br />This is a contribution towards Rich Westwood's Book of the Century meme at his <i>Past Offences</i> blog; this month <a href="https://pastoffences.wordpress.com/2015/06/01/1934book-sign-up-page/" rel="nofollow noopener">the year in question is 1934</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1480262674242869891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2530450821" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2530450821" />
    <a title="Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10818276-lee"><img alt="Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341872613p2/10818276.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2530450821?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee" href="/user/show/10818276-lee">Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=english">english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=cosy-mystery">cosy-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2530450821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12847511847777934407">New Zealand born Ngaio Marsh is one of the four ‘great ladies’ of mystery writing. This was her debut novel, first published in 1934. So, how does it hold up?<br/><br/>Mostly, it’s great. A lot of the language is outdated (the speech tag of ‘ejaculated’ made me flush each time I read it) but still easy enough to follow and quite fun. <br/><br/>The set up of the crime is inspired. A group of people attend a house party where they plan to play a murder mystery game. As in, one guest will become the corpse/victim, and</span>
  <span id="freeText12847511847777934407" style="display:none">New Zealand born Ngaio Marsh is one of the four ‘great ladies’ of mystery writing. This was her debut novel, first published in 1934. So, how does it hold up?<br /><br />Mostly, it’s great. A lot of the language is outdated (the speech tag of ‘ejaculated’ made me flush each time I read it) but still easy enough to follow and quite fun. <br /><br />The set up of the crime is inspired. A group of people attend a house party where they plan to play a murder mystery game. As in, one guest will become the corpse/victim, and the other guests will face the challenge of solving the crime/mystery and coming up with the murderer’s identity whilst they carry out a mock inquest. The game goes awry when the supposed pretend corpse is found truly dead. <br /><br />This book introduces us to Marsh’s Scotland Yard detective hero, Inspector Alleyn, who will go on to feature in a further 32 books of hers. I have read one other Alleyn book, Artists in Crime, and adored that and him, but I thought he was a little enigmatic (and erratic at times) in this novel. Not only do I put this down to being his debut but also because he doesn’t actually make an appearance into the story until around the 30% mark. <br /><br />Yes, Marsh was taking a gamble by not introducing her hero until later, but I still think things worked. Until then, we read from the point of view of young Nigel, a journalist who is one of the guests. Luckily Nigel, along with his potential new girlfriend, Angela, is quite an affable and likeable character. They have a real teenage sleuthing couple vibe going on. Of course, Marsh is clever enough to write the book in such a style that I couldn’t discount them completely from my list of suspects, keeping me on tenterhooks.<br /><br />Like all good mystery novels, everyone has a motive and most of them are pretty well telegraphed beforehand. There is no end of the book reveal of why the murderer carried out their crime. Instead, the end of the book reveal is how the murderer killed their victim. When this is revealed it’s quite original (although admittedly a little unbelievable).<br /> <br />The thing I didn’t like about the novel was the ‘Russian element’. It seems so ridiculous now, to read about evil Russian ‘brotherhoods’. It’s pretty much just a bit of racist paranoia. Of course, you have to remember the book was written in the 1930s. (And now Russian brotherhoods have probably been replaced by Muslim terrorist cells or something similar…) <br /><br />Apart from the racism of the Russian element, which I had to put down to its age, there's nothing offensive about the book. If you’re a fan of clean cosy mysteries, you should try this one.<br /> <br />All in all this is a solid start to a series and I’m looking forward to seeing how Marsh and Alleyn mature.<br /><br />4 out of 5</span>
  <a data-text-id="12847511847777934407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_748327977" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/748327977" />
    <a title="Nicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/223837-nicky"><img alt="Nicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/748327977?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer748327977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5181066642452326565">I'm not wildly enthused about Ngaio Marsh and Inspector Alleyn, at this point. It's a smooth enough read, but the murder is a little haphazardly imagined: some elements of it suggest premeditation, while others suggest a crime of opportunity, but it has to be one or the other or it just doesn't work. Too much depends on opportunity -- the availability of the weapon, the position of the murdered man, the way the murder game turns out -- and yet the rest of it smacks of pre-meditation: the bizarre</span>
  <span id="freeText5181066642452326565" style="display:none">I'm not wildly enthused about Ngaio Marsh and Inspector Alleyn, at this point. It's a smooth enough read, but the murder is a little haphazardly imagined: some elements of it suggest premeditation, while others suggest a crime of opportunity, but it has to be one or the other or it just doesn't work. Too much depends on opportunity -- the availability of the weapon, the position of the murdered man, the way the murder game turns out -- and yet the rest of it smacks of pre-meditation: the bizarre way the murderer sneaks downstairs to do it, planning out what gloves to use, arranging an alibi... And then there's the whole mess of the Russian secret society plot. Just... what?!<br /><br />I can't say I really cared much about any of the characters. Alleyn seems... weirdly mercurial, but not in a believable way, flipping personalities more often than you'd change clothes. I don't understand him a bit. And Nigel Bathgate is just too bland: a Watson type of sidekick who makes silly mistakes and can't figure anything out.<br /><br />I know I didn't like Peter Wimsey incredibly much the first time I read <i>Whose Body?</i>, so I'm giving this series more of a chance, but I'm not sure I'll go beyond the three books I have. So many books, so little time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5181066642452326565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1728873794" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1728873794" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14773738-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509454384p2/14773738.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1728873794?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/14773738-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14773738-julie?shelf=british">british</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14773738-julie?shelf=bumps-in-the-night">bumps-in-the-night</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14773738-julie?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1728873794" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer958746411535730397">As Ngaio Marsh's fledgling flight into the world of detective novels, this book had enough in it to pique my interest and leave the door open for more of her works. Although it lacks the mellifluous flow of Dame Agatha, in style, in writing, and in ideas, I found it still filled the gap for that "country-house cosy" that I was looking for.<br/><br/>There is a bit of a gimmicky feel to it overall as if Marsh is trying to capture Christie's style, and not quite succeeding, especially in Inspector Alleyn's c</span>
  <span id="freeText958746411535730397" style="display:none">As Ngaio Marsh's fledgling flight into the world of detective novels, this book had enough in it to pique my interest and leave the door open for more of her works. Although it lacks the mellifluous flow of Dame Agatha, in style, in writing, and in ideas, I found it still filled the gap for that "country-house cosy" that I was looking for.<br /><br />There is a bit of a gimmicky feel to it overall as if Marsh is trying to capture Christie's style, and not quite succeeding, especially in Inspector Alleyn's characterization. He's neither fish, nor fowl, nor good red herring in this novel -- and it shows -- but ends up being likeable enough nonetheless. <br /><br />There is also a bit of a haphazard feel to the plot: she doesn't seem quite sure about where she's going and leaves the reader somewhat befuddled at times. (As simple as the plot is, it was a bit hard to follow: like when you ask a child where he's been for the day, and he gives you a rambling tale about a dog, a sailboat, a monster and a purple rabbit.) Perhaps it is this quality which makes it all the more endearing, and in the end charming enough to want to read the second book in the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="958746411535730397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1533565808?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/2329228-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312963583" href="/book/show/835695.A_Man_Lay_Dead">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=detection-club">detection-club</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1533565808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9832376507165823432"><b>3.5</b><br/>I did not particularly enjoy the first half of this book. It started off like <i>Death of a Peer</i> (though thankfully the murder happens much sooner) with endless recounting of whereabouts and alibis. <br/>However, as the story progressed it became much more exciting. Russian secret societies, torrid affairs, and the subtle romance that seems to have died with the Golden Age of of Detection all blend together to create a fun, fast paced read. This is the Roderick Alleyn I was prepared to meet, complete</span>
  <span id="freeText9832376507165823432" style="display:none"><b>3.5</b><br />I did not particularly enjoy the first half of this book. It started off like <i>Death of a Peer</i> (though thankfully the murder happens much sooner) with endless recounting of whereabouts and alibis. <br />However, as the story progressed it became much more exciting. Russian secret societies, torrid affairs, and the subtle romance that seems to have died with the Golden Age of of Detection all blend together to create a fun, fast paced read. This is the Roderick Alleyn I was prepared to meet, complete with an elegant and shadowy past. It doesn't take Agatha Christie to figure out whodunit, but at the same time, it kept me guessing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9832376507165823432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_597941258" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/597941258" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5684259-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329866549p2/5684259.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/597941258?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/5684259-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer597941258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1066133252163409375">This was not particularly a good book. I had a difficult time trying to decide who was the main character and the mystery was pretty weak. It seemed that at the last minute the author randomly picked one of the characters to be the murderer and then came up with some unconvincing clues to tie it all together. And there was an unrelated Russian crime ring randomly thrown in. <br/><br/>I'm going to attempt a few more of her books because I adore all sorts of English mysteries and Ngaio Marsh is well loved b</span>
  <span id="freeText1066133252163409375" style="display:none">This was not particularly a good book. I had a difficult time trying to decide who was the main character and the mystery was pretty weak. It seemed that at the last minute the author randomly picked one of the characters to be the murderer and then came up with some unconvincing clues to tie it all together. And there was an unrelated Russian crime ring randomly thrown in. <br /><br />I'm going to attempt a few more of her books because I adore all sorts of English mysteries and Ngaio Marsh is well loved by many. I'm hoping it just took her a book or two to get good. </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2964711304" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2964711304" />
    <a title="Greg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39346323-greg"><img alt="Greg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513962691p2/39346323.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2964711304?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greg" href="/user/show/39346323-greg">Greg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2964711304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4110620110818888461">Dame Agatha Christie and her Peers<br/>BOOK 10<br/>CAST – 3 stars: Inspector Alleyn is quick on the scene. We learn little about him in this first outing but when he says, “…I have known for some time…I find there is often a moment in a case when a piece of one’s mind…knows the end while the rest of the trained brain cuts this intuitive bit dead,” one can’t help but flash to Christie’s famous Hercule Poirot and his ‘brain cells ‘ at work. I’m not sure if this is an attempt to differentiate Alleyn from Poi</span>
  <span id="freeText4110620110818888461" style="display:none">Dame Agatha Christie and her Peers<br />BOOK 10<br />CAST – 3 stars: Inspector Alleyn is quick on the scene. We learn little about him in this first outing but when he says, “…I have known for some time…I find there is often a moment in a case when a piece of one’s mind…knows the end while the rest of the trained brain cuts this intuitive bit dead,” one can’t help but flash to Christie’s famous Hercule Poirot and his ‘brain cells ‘ at work. I’m not sure if this is an attempt to differentiate Alleyn from Poirot, or if it’s a tribute, but either way Marsh owes Christie a debt of gratitude for inspiration. Nigel Bathgate is a journalist on holiday and is a cousin of Charles Rankin, who seems to be courting Miss Rosamund Grant (a tall, dark, beauty). Mrs. Marjorie Wilde's best asset appears to be her large blue eyes. Mr. Arthur Wilde might know of his wife’s dalliances, but no matter as he defends her throughout the novel. Sir Hubert Handesley is a very handsome, rich 50-year-old with white hair (my, how people used to age fast…) and appears to be a 'confirmed bachelor.' Dr. Foma Torkareff is from Petrograd and knows Handesley from an embassy meeting. Then there is a Russian Brotherhood “..of amazing antiquity and was strong in the reign of Peter the Great, when it practiced various indecent and horrible rites…”. Yea, I admit, I wanted to know more about the indecent rites but alas, nary a single indecent rite is revealed. There is a Russian butler, Vassilly, dedicated to Sir Hubert. Angela North, Sir Hubert’s niece, wraps up the main cast. It’s a good cast, but only little Sissy provides the best line: “Loidies don’t go wiv loidies in der coppus (or coppice, according to her father).” Unfortunately, Sissy has nothing to do with the story, but she surely knows who is going with who deep into the forest. Another line of immense interest from lawyer Benningden goes: “Your cousin’s relationships with women were, shall we say, of a slightly ephemeral nature…” Now that’s a new one for me, ‘ephemeral nature.’ Still, message received loud and clear! But then, as it turns out, that’s not the case at all! The cast is average.<br />PLOT/CRIME – 3: The victim is stabbed in the back with a Mongolian dagger during a weekend house party. The cast is playing a “Murder Game” in which a character is giving a silver plaque indicating they’ll play the part of the murderer and they are to tap someone and say “You’re dead” or something to that effect. Then, later, there’ll be a trial. Naturally, the game becomes real. Very interesting! (Of late -September of 2019 - I've seen an ad for a film in which a "Murder Game" is played, but the ad tells us up front that, all along, the victim is a woman about to be married and the family doesn't care for their 'new' family member. So, might as well skip that film.) Much is made of the dagger, the source of the dagger, its appearance, etc. But this "Murder Game" was already a country house staple by the time this book was written.<br />PLACE/ATMOSPHERE – 2: Most of the action takes place at Frantock, Sir Hubert’s country home. Here again, I must mention Dame Agatha, the master of the ‘country manor house weekend party’ and relativity strikes! Never are we told much about Frantock, other than it is of ‘old brick.’ Very disappointing! Why, new American houses are often finished by covering wood frames with used 'old brick.' At least the action in and among the trees of the forest is interesting and...well, questionable. Who, exactly, is doing who and why are people taking other people's trousers down and...oh, this book has some odd features. Have a drink every time someone says, "Let's go play in the forest" or every time the author winks at us.<br />INVESTIGATION –1: Inspector Alleyn and his Latermen, of course, question everyone in the house, all the while insisting the murderer might have come from outside. The elongated interview with the previously mentioned Sissy is, well, way too long and is aimed only for Sissy’s great exit line, but that’s forgivable: the set-up was worth it. The action moves quickly to a second murder (natch), an arrest, to a restaurant and to Alleyn’s own home in which one cast member is tortured, pointlessly. (The violence is surprisingly vicious.) Then we head back to Frantock, where the first murder is acted out. But Alleyn has little to no possible knowledge other than backward fingerprints on the wrong side of a stairway post and this is a huge flaw because the…<br />SOLUTION (does it even deserve 1 star?) …is stupendously ridiculous. There is no way the victim and the murderer could possibly have been in the positions in which the murder occurs. It’s actually laughable. Think "Hide and Seek" and "Twister". And adults DON’T DO THIS! And IF they did, it is ridiculously silly that the murder weapon is within reach and, get this, the victim is in just the right position, and it’s the exact person the murderer is after because ANYONE could have been bent over and in that same position. It’s a case where the author seemingly thought up a scenario of the murder and then wrote backwards, and it just doesn’t work. It would have been impossible for the murderer to plan this and to have all the pieces fall in place. And when Inspector Alleyn informs his prime witness (the person he knows didn’t do it) that what the witness saw/heard was absolutely wrong and virtually impossible, you know things have gone off track and the author has withheld a clue(s) and not played ‘fair.’ That said, the chapter in which this 'solution' takes place is titled “Alleyn Comes Cleanish”, so the author does admit, in a way, that withheld clues appear late in the game. (I'll give the solution 1 star for creativity.)<br />SUMMARY: 2.0 overall. I’ll quote the back cover’s statements about Ngaio Marsh and this novel: “…her oeuvre opens with, yes, a country-house party between the two world wars-servants bustling, gin flowing, the gentlemen in dinner jackets, the ladies all slink and smolder.” If ONLY there had been more slink and smolder! The cast is fine, the plot/crime could have been very good in and of itself, IF it had ultimately been believable, but this novel is lacking in atmosphere and falls apart completely at the ‘big reveal’. This author is rather famous, so one can only assume her prowess as a mystery writer improves. I can think of dozens of ways to do away with someone far easier...and still be in the dark with a very sharp dagger.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4110620110818888461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('F/yaApBWRJUArGZ/YRvTTtopqrqQJ0Nwjjinx2HBQkVJAUk+HTAV/McXYtlYqHKdKWgk8U5Sd8bcNyjPJ80jgg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('N2IQhYbuxY1Yi/cbwTIY2bzHacAKUq3wQrlATGaHD8Fpn8O5C4iU5J8w8734gbkKT4bni9QnmUYQts9EIItuBg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1529555517851200657">Dame Ngaio Marsh, born Edith Ngaio Marsh, was a New Zealand crime writer and theatre director. There is some uncertainty over her birth date as her father neglected to register her birth until 1900, but she was born in the city of Christchurch, New Zealand.<br/><br/>Of all the "Great Ladies" of the English mystery's golden age, including Margery Allingham, Agatha Christie, and Dorothy L. Sayers, Ngaio Marsh</span>
  <span id="freeText1529555517851200657" style="display:none">Dame Ngaio Marsh, born Edith Ngaio Marsh, was a New Zealand crime writer and theatre director. There is some uncertainty over her birth date as her father neglected to register her birth until 1900, but she was born in the city of Christchurch, New Zealand.<br /><br />Of all the "Great Ladies" of the English mystery's golden age, including Margery Allingham, Agatha Christie, and Dorothy L. Sayers, Ngaio Marsh alone survived to publish in the 1980s. Over a fifty-year span, from 1932 to 1982, Marsh wrote thirty-two classic English detective novels, which gained international acclaim. She did not always see herself as a writer, but first planned a career as a painter.<br /><br />Marsh's first novel, A MAN LAY DEAD (1934), which she wrote in London in 1931-32, introduced the detective Inspector Roderick Alleyn: a combination of Sayers's Lord Peter Wimsey and a realistically depicted police official at work. Throughout the 1930s Marsh painted occasionally, wrote plays for local repertory societies in New Zealand, and published detective novels. In 1937 Marsh went to England for a period. Before going back to her home country, she spent six months travelling about Europe. <br /><br />All her novels feature British CID detective Roderick Alleyn. Several novels feature Marsh's other loves, the theatre and painting. A number are set around theatrical productions (Enter a Murderer, Vintage Murder, Overture to Death, Opening Night, Death at the Dolphin, and Light Thickens), and two others are about actors off stage (Final Curtain and False Scent). Her short story "'I Can Find My Way Out" is also set around a theatrical production and is the earlier "Jupiter case" referred to in Opening Night. Alleyn marries a painter, Agatha Troy, whom he meets during an investigation (Artists in Crime), and who features in several later novels.<br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/50710-roderick-alleyn" rel="nofollow noopener">Roderick Alleyn</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1529555517851200657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
